\t\tacpi_video_unregister_backlight();\n384: }\n385: \n386: static int acpi_video_backlight_notify(struct notifier_block *nb,\n387: \t\t\t\t       unsigned long val, void *bd)\n388: {\n389: \tstruct {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01TDxKycx2Fvutg6jRxGLARr","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"I see! The `video_set_backlight_video_vendor` callback disables the Acer WMI brightness capability. This means those devices should use the generic video driver (acpi-video or native) instead of the acer-wmi driver.\n\nNow, based on the bug report:1. **Without any quirk** - the device defaults to using intel_backlight from the GPU driver, which doesn't work\n2. **With `acpi_backlight=vendor`** - it tries to use acer-wmi, which also doesn't work\n3. **With `acpi_backlight=native`** - it uses the native ACPI video backlight, which works\n\nThis means the TravelMate 5735Z needs to be configured to use native backlight. Looking at the available options:1. Add it to `video_detect_dmi_table` in `drivers/acpi/video_detect.c` with `video_detect_force_native` callback - this would make the kernel prefer native backlight\n2. Add it to `video_vendor_dmi_table` in `drivers/platform/x86/acer-wmi.c` - but this only disables acer-wmi, it doesn't force native\n\nActually, thinking about it more carefully. The issue might be that:- The TravelMate 5735Z might have ACPI video backlight support, but the default auto-detection is not choosing native backlight- Or it's choosing the wrong driver\n\nLet me re-read the bug report more carefully. The bug says:- \"trying to change the brightness of the internal display using the function keys, GNOME shows the OSD, which seems to have five levels (from acer_wmi?), but the actual brightness does not change\"\n- \"Booting the system with `acpi_backlight=vendor`, exposes `/sys/devices/platform/acer-wmi/backlight/acer-wmi/brightness`, but the behavior is the same\"\n\n\n- With `acpi_backlight=native`, the function keys work properly and expose 15 or 16 brightness levels instead of five.\n\nThe pattern is clear: intel_backlight fails, acer-wmi fails, but native ACPI video succeeds. The brightness OSD appears when using function keys, but the actual brightness does not change.\n\n### Root Cause\nThe device is missing an entry in the DMI quirks table that determines which backlight backend the kernel should use. The auto-detection selects an incorrect backlight driver.\n\n### Evidence\n- **Default behavior**: intel_backlight appears but doesn't work\n- **With acpi_backlight=vendor**: acer-wmi backlight appears but still doesn't work\n- **With acpi_backlight=native**: Native ACPI video backlight works correctly and shows 15-16 brightness levels\n\n### Solution\nAdd the device to the device.\n\nThe fix would add something like:\n```c\n{\n  .callback = video_detect_force_native,\n  .ident = \"Acer TravelMate 5735Z\",\n  .matches = {\n    DMI_MATCH(DMI_SYS_VENDOR, \"Acer\"),\n    DMI_MATCH(DMI_PRODUCT_NAME, \"TravelMate 5735Z\"),\n  },\n},\n```\n\nThis is a device-specific quirk that tells the kernel to use native backlight for this particular laptop model, matching the
